played.[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-164) Winning La Liga for the [2017–18](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_FC_Barcelona_season "2017–18 FC Barcelona season") season, on 9 May 2018, Barcelona defeated Villarreal 5–1 to set the [longest unbeaten streak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Liga_records_and_statistics#Games_without_a_loss "La Liga records and statistics") (43 games) in La Liga history.[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-165) On 27 April 2019, Barcelona won their 26th La Liga title.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-166) However, the La Liga title was overshadowed by an improbable [Champions League exit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_phase#Semi-finals "2018–19 UEFA Champions League knockout phase") to Liverpool in the semi-finals, with Barça losing the second leg 0–4 after being up 3–0 after a home victory.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-167)
On 13 January 2020, following the loss to Atlético Madrid in the [Spanish Supercup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Supercopa_de_Espa%C3%B1a "2019–20 Supercopa de España"), former [Real Betis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Betis "Real Betis") coach [Quique Setién](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quique_Seti%C3%A9n "Quique Setién") replaced Ernesto Valverde as the new head coach of Barcelona.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-168) Ultimately Barcelona finished the season trophyless for first time in 12 years. On 17 August, the club confirmed that Setién had been removed from his position as manager with [director of football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Director_of_football "Director of football") [Eric Abidal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Abidal "Eric Abidal") also dismissed from his position.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-169) Two days later, [Ronald Koeman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Koeman "Ronald Koeman") was appointed as the new head coach of Barcelona.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-170) Rising dissatisfaction among supporters due to worsening finances and decline on the pitch in the previous season led to Josep Maria Bartomeu announcing his resignation as president on 27 October 2020, to avoid facing a vote of no confidence from the club members.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-171)[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-172)
### 2021–present: Return of Laporta and post-Messi era
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/F%C3%BAtbol_Club_Barcelona_league_performance_1929-present.svg/960px-F%C3%BAtbol_Club_Barcelona_league_performance_1929-present.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:F%C3%BAtbol_Club_Barcelona_league_performance_1929-present.svg)Chart of Barcelona's league performance 1929–2023
On 7 March 2021, Joan Laporta was elected president of Barcelona with 54.28% of the vote.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-173) Barcelona won their 31st Copa del Rey, their only trophy under Ronald Koeman, after defeating Athletic Bilbao 4–0 in the [final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Copa_del_Rey_Final "2021 Copa del Rey Final").[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-174) In August 2021 Barcelona found themselves unable to comply with La Liga's Financial Fair Play requirements, and revealed a club debt of €1.35bn and a wage bill accounting for 103% of total income. Negotiations with Lionel Messi, now in the final year of his contract, had been ongoing for some time. However, on 5 August 2021, Barcelona announced that they would be unable to re-sign Messi to an extension due to La Liga regulations. This was despite the fact that the club and Messi had reached an agreement over the details of a new contract. Messi departed the club after 21 years as a Barça player, and the club's all-time leading goalscorer, and signed on a free transfer with French club [Paris Saint-Germain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain "Paris Saint-Germain").[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-175)[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-176) The financial implications also restricted Barcelona in the transfer market and as a result most of the incoming players were either free transfers or loans and they had to reduce players' wages to register the incoming players.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-177)
Poor performances in [La Liga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_La_Liga "2021–22 La Liga") and the [Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_UEFA_Champions_League "2021–22 UEFA Champions League") led to the sacking of Ronald Koeman on 28 October, with a club legend [Xavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xavi_\(footballer,_born_1980\) "Xavi \(footballer, born 1980\)") replacing him.[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-178)[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-179) Xavi could not reverse the fortunes in the Champions League, and Barcelona dropped down to the [Europa League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_UEFA_Europa_League "2021–22 UEFA Europa League") for the first time since [2003–04](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_FC_Barcelona_season "2003–04 FC Barcelona season"), subsequently exiting in the quarter-finals.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-180) In the domestic league, Xavi improved Barça's form and guided them from ninth to second, guaranteeing a Champions League spot next season. However, this also meant Barcelona finished trophyless after earlier Supercopa and Copa del Rey exits.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-181)
On 15 January 2023, Xavi guided Barcelona to their first trophy since the [2021 Copa del Rey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Copa_del_Rey "2020–21 Copa del Rey"), as the Catalans defeated Real Madrid 3–1 in the [Supercopa de España](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022%E2%80%9323_Supercopa_de_Espa%C3%B1a "2022–23 Supercopa de España") [final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_Supercopa_de_Espa%C3%B1a_Final "2023 Supercopa de España Final").[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-182) On 14 May 2023, Barcelona mathematically clinched their [27th league title](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022%E2%80%9323_La_Liga "2022–23 La Liga") with four games to spare, the first in the post-Messi era.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-183)
## Support
Main article: [Supporters of FC Barcelona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supporters_of_FC_Barcelona "Supporters of FC Barcelona")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/El_Camp_Nou_en_un_partido_de_la_Uefa_Champions_League.jpg/250px-El_Camp_Nou_en_un_partido_de_la_Uefa_Champions_League.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:El_Camp_Nou_en_un_partido_de_la_Uefa_Champions_League.jpg)[Tifo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tifo "Tifo") at Camp Nou in a 2013 [comeback](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comeback_\(sports\)#Association_football "Comeback \(sports\)") against AC Milan
The nickname _culer_ for a Barcelona supporter is derived from the Catalan _cul_ (English: arse), as the spectators at the first stadium, Camp de la Indústria, sat with their _culs_ over the stand.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-184)[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-185) In Spain, about 25% of the population is said to be Barça sympathisers, second behind Real Madrid, supported by 32% of the population.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-186) Throughout Europe, Barcelona is the favourite second-choice club.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-187) The club's membership figures have seen a significant increase from 100,000 in the 2003–04 season to 170,000 in September 2009,[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-socis-188) the sharp rise being attributed to the influence of Ronaldinho and then-president Joan Laporta's media strategy that focused on Spanish and English online media.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-189)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-190) As of 31 May 2023[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=FC_Barcelona&action=edit), the club has 150,317 memberships, called _socis_.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-xavison-191)
In addition to membership, as of March 2022[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=FC_Barcelona&action=edit) there are 1,264 officially registered fan clubs, called _penyes_ , around the world.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-192) The fan clubs promote Barcelona in their locality and receive beneficial offers when visiting Barcelona.[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-193) Among the best supported teams globally, Barcelona has the second highest social media following in the world among sports teams, with over 103 million Facebook fans as of December 2021[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=FC_Barcelona&action=edit), only behind Real Madrid with 111 million.[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-Social_media-12)[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-194) The club has had many prominent people among its supporters, including Pope [John Paul II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Paul_II "John Paul II"), who was an honorary member, and former prime minister of Spain [José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero "José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero").[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-195)[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-196)
## Club rivalries
### _El Clásico_
Main article: [El Clásico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Cl%C3%A1sico "El Clásico")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Forcejeo_Real_Madrid_-_FC_Barcelona.jpg/250px-Forcejeo_Real_Madrid_-_FC_Barcelona.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Forcejeo_Real_Madrid_-_FC_Barcelona.jpg)Players jostle in Barcelona's 2–6 win against Real Madrid at the [Santiago Bernabéu Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium "Santiago Bernabéu Stadium") in a 2009 _El Clásico_.
There is often a fierce rivalry between the two strongest teams in a national league, and this is particularly the case in La Liga, where the game between Barcelona and [Real Madrid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF "Real Madrid CF") is known as "The Classic" (_El Clásico_). From the start of national competitions the clubs were seen as representatives of two rival regions in Spain: [Catalonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalonia "Catalonia") and [Castile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castile_\(historical_region\) "Castile \(historical region\)"), as well as of the two cities. The rivalry reflects what many regard as the political and cultural tensions felt between [Catalans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalan_people "Catalan people") and the [Castilians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castilians "Castilians"), seen by one author as a re-enactment of the [Spanish Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War "Spanish Civil War").[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-197) Over the years, the head-to-head record between the two clubs is 102 victories for Madrid, 100 victories for Barcelona, and 52 draws.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Camp_Nou_during_El_Clasico_October_2012.jpg/250px-Camp_Nou_during_El_Clasico_October_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Camp_Nou_during_El_Clasico_October_2012.jpg)Barcelona fans creating a mosaic of the [Catalan flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senyera "Senyera") before a 2012 _El Clasico_ at Camp Nou
As early as the 1930s, Barcelona "had developed a reputation as a symbol of Catalan identity, opposed to the centralising tendencies of Madrid".[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-josepsunyol-198)[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-199) In 1936, when [Francisco Franco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francisco_Franco "Francisco Franco") started the _[Coup d'état](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "Coup d'état")_ against the democratic [Second Spanish Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic "Second Spanish Republic"), the president of Barcelona, [Josep Sunyol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Sunyol "Josep Sunyol"), member of the [Republican Left of Catalonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Left_of_Catalonia "Republican Left of Catalonia") and Deputy to [The Cortes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cortes_Generales "Cortes Generales"), was arrested and executed without trial by Franco's troops[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-McNeillp261-200) (Sunyol was exercising his political activities, visiting Republican troops north of Madrid).[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-josepsunyol-198) During the dictatorships of [Miguel Primo de Rivera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miguel_Primo_de_Rivera "Miguel Primo de Rivera") and especially [Francisco Franco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francoist_Spain "Francoist Spain"), all regional languages and identities in Spain were frowned upon and restrained. As such, most citizens of Barcelona were in strong opposition to the fascist-like regime. In this period, Barcelona gained their motto _Més que un club_ (_English: More than a club_) because of its alleged connection to [Catalan nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalan_nationalism "Catalan nationalism") as well as to [progressive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressivism "Progressivism") beliefs.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-201)
There's an ongoing controversy as to what extent Franco's rule (1939–75) influenced the activities and on-pitch results of both Barcelona and Real Madrid. Fans of both clubs tend to exaggerate the myths favouring their narratives. Most historians agree than Franco did not have a preferred football team, but his Spanish nationalist beliefs led him to associate himself with the establishment teams, such as [Atlético Aviación](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid "Atlético Madrid") and [Madrid FC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF "Real Madrid CF") (that recovered its _royal_ name after the fall of the Republic). On the other hand, he also wanted the renamed _CF Barcelona_ succeed as "Spanish team" rather than a Catalan one. During the early years of Franco's rule, Real Madrid were not particularly successful, winning two [Copa del Generalísimo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copa_del_Rey "Copa del Rey") titles and a [Copa Eva Duarte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copa_Eva_Duarte "Copa Eva Duarte"); Barcelona claimed three [league titles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Spanish_football_champions "List of Spanish football champions"), one Copa del Generalísimo and one Copa Eva Duarte. During that period, Atlético Aviación were believed to be the preferred team over Real Madrid. The most contested stories of the period include Real Madrid's 11–1 home win against Barcelona in the [Copa del Generalísimo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1943_Copa_del_General%C3%ADsimo "1943 Copa del Generalísimo"), where the Catalan team alleged intimidation, and the controversial transfer of [Alfredo Di Stéfano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano "Alfredo Di Stéfano") to Real Madrid despite his agreement with Barcelona. The latter transfer was part of Real Madrid chairman [Santiago Bernabéu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_\(footballer\) "Santiago Bernabéu \(footballer\)")'s "revolution" that ushered in the era of unprecedented dominance. Bernabéu, himself a veteran of the Civil War who fought for [Franco's forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist_faction_\(Spanish_Civil_War\) "Nationalist faction \(Spanish Civil War\)"), saw Real Madrid on top not only of Spanish but also European football, helping create the [European Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League "UEFA Champions League"), the first true competition for Europe's best club sides. His vision was fulfilled when Real Madrid not only started winning consecutive league titles but also swept the first five editions of the European Cup in the 1950s.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-202) These events had a profound impact on Spanish football and influenced Franco's attitude. According to historians, during this time he realized the importance of Real Madrid for his regime's international image, and the club became his preferred team until his death. [Fernando Maria Castiella](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fernando_Maria_Castiella "Fernando Maria Castiella"), who served as [Minister of Foreign Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_\(Spain\) "Minister of Foreign Affairs \(Spain\)") under Franco from 1957 until 1969, noted that "[Real Madrid] is the best embassy we have ever had." Franco died in 1975, and the [Spanish transition to democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy "Spanish transition to democracy") soon followed. Under his rule, [Real Madrid had won](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Real_Madrid_CF_records_and_statistics#Honours "List of Real Madrid CF records and statistics") 14 league titles, 6 Copa del Generalísimo titles, 1 Copa Eva Duarte, 6 European Cups, 2 [Latin Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_Cup "Latin Cup"), and 1 [Intercontinental Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_\(1960%E2%80%932004\) "Intercontinental Cup \(1960–2004\)"). In the same period, [Barcelona had won](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FC_Barcelona_records_and_statistics#Honours "List of FC Barcelona records and statistics") 8 league titles, 9 Copa del Generalísimo titles, 3 Copa Eva Duarte titles, 3 [Inter-Cities Fairs Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inter-Cities_Fairs_Cup "Inter-Cities Fairs Cup"), and 2 Latin Cups.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-203)[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-204)
The rivalry was intensified during the 1950s when the clubs disputed the signing of [Alfredo Di Stéfano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano "Alfredo Di Stéfano"). Di Stéfano had impressed both Barcelona and Real Madrid while playing for [Los Millionarios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Los_Millonarios "Club Deportivo Los Millonarios") in [Bogotá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1 "Bogotá"), Colombia, during a players' strike in his native [Argentina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argentina "Argentina"). Soon after Millonarios' return to Colombia, Barcelona directors visited Buenos Aires and agreed with River Plate, the last FIFA-affiliated team to have held Di Stéfano's rights, for his transfer in 1954 for the equivalent of 150 million Italian lira (according to other sources 200,000 dollars). This started a battle between the two Spanish rivals for his rights. FIFA appointed Armando Muñoz Calero, former president of the Spanish Football Federation as mediator. Calero decided to let Di Stéfano play the 1953–54 and 1955–56 seasons in Madrid, and the 1954–55 and 1956–57 seasons in Barcelona. The agreement was approved by the Football Association and their respective clubs. Although the Catalans agreed, the decision created various discontent among the Blaugrana members and the president was forced to resign in September 1953. Barcelona sold Madrid their half-share, and Di Stéfano moved to _Los Blancos_ , signing a four-year contract. Real paid 5.5 million Spanish pesetas for the transfer, plus a 1.3 million bonus for the purchase, an annual fee to be paid to the Millonarios, and a 16,000 salary for Di Stéfano with a bonus double that of his teammates, for a total of 40% of the annual revenue of the Madrid club.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-di_Stefano-205)
Di Stéfano became integral in the subsequent success achieved by Real Madrid, scoring twice in his first game against Barcelona. With him, Madrid won the first five editions of the [European Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League "UEFA Champions League").[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-206) The 1960s saw the rivalry reach the European stage when Real Madrid and Barcelona met twice in the European Cup, with Madrid triumphing en route to their fifth consecutive title in [1959–60](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1959%E2%80%9360_European_Cup "1959–60 European Cup") and Barcelona prevailing en route to losing the final in [1960–61](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1960%E2%80%9361_European_Cup "1960–61 European Cup"). In 2002, the European encounter between the clubs was dubbed the "Match of The Century" by Spanish media, and Madrid's win was watched by more than 500 million people.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-207) An intense fixture which is marked by its indiscipline in addition to [memorable goal celebrations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goal_celebration "Goal celebration") from both teams – often involving mocking the opposition – such notable celebrations occurred in 2009 when Barcelona captain [Carles Puyol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carles_Puyol "Carles Puyol") kissed his Catalan armband in front of incensed Madrid fans at the [Santiago Bernabéu Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium "Santiago Bernabéu Stadium") and in 2017 when Lionel Messi celebrated his 93rd-minute winner for Barcelona against Real Madrid at the Bernabéu by taking off his Barcelona shirt and holding it up to incensed Real Madrid fans – with his name and number facing them.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-208)
### _El derbi Barceloní_
Main article: [Derbi Barceloní](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Derbi_Barcelon%C3%AD "Derbi Barceloní")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/FC_Barcelona_vs_RCD_Espanyol_%282005-06%29_%2858%29_%28142178805%29.jpg/250px-FC_Barcelona_vs_RCD_Espanyol_%282005-06%29_%2858%29_%28142178805%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:FC_Barcelona_vs_RCD_Espanyol_\(2005-06\)_\(58\)_\(142178805\).jpg)Barcelona players parade La Liga trophy around Camp Nou in May 2006 after defeating [Espanyol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RCD_Espanyol "RCD Espanyol") in their last home game of the season.
Barça's local rival has always been [Espanyol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RCD_Espanyol "RCD Espanyol"). _Blanc-i-blaus_ , being one of the clubs granted royal patronage, was founded exclusively by Spanish football fans, unlike the multinational nature of Barça's primary board. The founding message of the club was clearly anti-Barcelona, and they disapprovingly saw FC Barcelona as a team of foreigners.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-Ball,_Phil._pp._86-87-209) The rivalry was strengthened by what Catalonians saw as a provocative representative of Madrid.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-210) Their original ground was in the affluent district of [Sarrià](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estadi_de_Sarri%C3%A0 "Estadi de Sarrià").[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-211)[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-212)
Traditionally, Espanyol was seen by the vast majority of Barcelona's citizens as a club which cultivated a kind of compliance to the central authority, in stark contrast to Barça's revolutionary spirit.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-213) Also in the 1960s and 1970s, while FC Barcelona acted as an integrating force for Catalonia's new arrivals from poorer regions of Spain expecting to find a better life, Espanyol drew their support mainly from sectors close to the [regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franco_regime "Franco regime") such as policemen, military officers, civil servants and career fascists.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-214)
In 1918, Espanyol started a counter-petition against autonomy, which at that time had become a pertinent issue.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-Ball,_Phil._pp._86-87-209) Later on, an Espanyol supporter group would join the Falangists in the Spanish Civil War, siding with the fascists. Despite these differences in ideology, the _derbi_ has always been more relevant to Espanyol supporters than Barcelona ones due to the difference in objectives. In recent years the rivalry has become less political, as Espanyol translated its official name and anthem from Spanish to Catalan.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-Ball,_Phil._pp._86-87-209)
Though it is the most played local derby in the history of La Liga, it is also the most unbalanced, with Barcelona overwhelmingly [dominant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_derbi_barcelones#Head_to_Head "El derbi barcelones"). In the primera división league table, Espanyol has only managed to end above Barça on three occasions from 87 seasons (1928–2022) and the only all-Catalan Copa del Rey final was won by Barça [in 1957](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1957_Copa_del_General%C3%ADsimo_Final "1957 Copa del Generalísimo Final"). Espanyol has the consolation of achieving the largest margin win with a 6–0 in 1951, while Barcelona's biggest win was 5–0 on seven occasions (in 1933, 1947, 1964, 1975, 1992, 2016 and 2017). Espanyol achieved a 2–1 win against Barça during the 2008–09 season, becoming the first team to defeat Barcelona at Camp Nou in their treble-winning [season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_FC_Barcelona_season "2008–09 FC Barcelona season").[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-215)
### Rivalry with AC Milan
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Milan_-_Barca_2006.jpg/250px-Milan_-_Barca_2006.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Milan_-_Barca_2006.jpg)Barcelona's ultras _[Boixos Nois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boixos_Nois "Boixos Nois")_ in the [2005–06 UEFA Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Champions_League "2005–06 UEFA Champions League") semi-final against [AC Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.C._Milan "A.C. Milan") at [San Siro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Siro "San Siro")
One of Barcelona's rivals in European football is Italian club AC Milan.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-216)[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-217)[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-218)[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-219) The team against which Barcelona has played the most matches (19), it is also the third most played match in European club competitions, behind Real Madrid–Juventus (21) and Real Madrid–Bayern Munich (26).[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-220)[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-221)[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-222) Two of the most successful clubs in Europe, Milan has won seven European Cups to Barça's five, while both clubs have won a record five European Super Cups.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-223) Barcelona and Milan have won other continental titles, which make them the second and third most decorated teams in world football, with 19 and 14 titles respectively, both behind Real Madrid's 23.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-224)
Barcelona leads the head-to-head record with eight wins and five defeats. The first encounter between the two clubs was in the [1959–60 European Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1959%E2%80%9360_European_Cup "1959–60 European Cup"). They faced off in the round of 16 and Barça won the tie on a 7–1 aggregate score (0–2 in Milan and 5–1 in Barcelona).[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-225) While Milan had never knocked Barcelona out of the European Cup, they beat Johan Cruyff's Dream Team 4–0 in the [1994 Champions League final](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1994_UEFA_Champions_League_Final "1994 UEFA Champions League Final"), despite being the underdogs.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-226)[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-227) In 2013, however, Barcelona made a "historic" comeback from a 0–2 first leg defeat in the round of 16 of the [2012–13 Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League "2012–13 UEFA Champions League"), winning 4–0 at Camp Nou.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-228)[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-229)
## Ownership and finances
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Civil_Guards_Socis_Camp_Industria.jpg/250px-Civil_Guards_Socis_Camp_Industria.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Civil_Guards_Socis_Camp_Industria.jpg)[Civil Guards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_Guard_\(Spain\) "Civil Guard \(Spain\)") at the _socis_ ' entrance of the [Camp de la Indústria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_de_la_Ind%C3%BAstria "Camp de la Indústria")
Along with Real Madrid, Athletic Bilbao, and [Osasuna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CA_Osasuna "CA Osasuna"), Barcelona is organised as a [registered association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nonprofit_organization "Nonprofit organization").[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-230)[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-231) Unlike a [limited company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Limited_company "Limited company"), it is not possible to purchase shares in the club, but only membership.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-232) The members of Barcelona, called _socis_ , form an assembly of delegates which is the highest governing body of the club.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-233) As of 31 May 2023[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=FC_Barcelona&action=edit), the club has 150,317 _socis_.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-xavison-191)
In 2010, _[Forbes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")_ evaluated Barcelona's worth to be around €752 million (US$1 billion), ranking them fourth after Manchester United, Real Madrid and Arsenal, based on figures from the 2008–09 season.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-234)[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-235) According to [Deloitte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deloitte "Deloitte"), Barcelona had a recorded revenue of €366 million in the same period, ranking second to Real Madrid, who generated €401 million in revenue.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-236) In 2013, _Forbes_ magazine ranked Barcelona the third most valuable sports team in the world, behind Real Madrid and Manchester United, with a value of $2.6 billion.[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-Forbes-237) In 2014, _Forbes_ ranked them the second most valuable sports team in the world, worth $3.2 billion, and Deloitte ranked them the world's fourth richest football club in terms of revenue, with an annual turnover of €484.6 million.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-Deloitte-238)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-Forbes_2014-239) In 2017, _Forbes_ ranked them the fourth most valuable sports team in the world with a team value of $3.64 billion.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-Forbes_2017-240) In 2018, Barcelona became the first sports team to surpass $1bn in annual revenues.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-FT2021-241) In November 2018 Barcelona became the first sports team with average first-team pay in excess of £10m ($13.8m) per year.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-242)[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-243) However, years of profligate spending under the leadership of [Josep Maria Bartomeu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Maria_Bartomeu "Josep Maria Bartomeu") (president between 2014 and 2020) and other factors, such as the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic"), saw the club's gross debt rise to about $1.4 billion in 2021, much of it short-term.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-FT2021-241)
On November 9, 2024, Barcelona announced its new sponsorship deal with Nike. It is said that it is the highest deal in football history.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-244)
## In popular culture
Since its origins, Barcelona has had a close relationship with the world of [culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture "Culture"), especially, with [Catalan culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalans#Culture_and_society "Catalans").[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-245)[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-246)[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-247) The club's statutes from 1932 already said that Barça "is an association of a cultural and sporting nature".[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-248) The club and [its players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FC_Barcelona_players "List of FC Barcelona players") have been a source of inspiration for [writers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Writer "Writer"), [musicians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musician "Musician"), [visual artists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_arts "Visual arts"), [journalists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Journalist "Journalist"), [cartoonists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cartoonist "Cartoonist"), [theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theatre "Theatre"), and [film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filmmaking "Filmmaking") people.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-249)[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-250)
In [literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literature "Literature"), some great [Catalan writers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Catalan-language_writers "List of Catalan-language writers") they were inspired by the club. In 1957, on the occasion of the inauguration of the [Camp Nou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_Nou "Camp Nou"), [Josep Maria de Sagarra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Maria_de_Sagarra "Josep Maria de Sagarra") dedicated a poem titled _Blau i grana_.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-251) [Poet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poet "Poet") [Manuel Vázquez Montalbán](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_V%C3%A1zquez_Montalb%C3%A1n "Manuel Vázquez Montalbán") wrote regularly about his vision of the team. Some expressions emerged that caught on in the popular imagination, such as identifying Barça with "The unarmed army of Catalonia." He also wrote that "Barça is the only legal institution that unites the man on the street with the Catalonia that could have been and was not."[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-252)[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-253)
The great anniversaries have been favorable occasions for the club to involve great Catalan figures from the cultural world in its activities. Names such as [Josep Segrelles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Segrelles "José Segrelles"), [Joan Miró](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_Mir%C3%B3 "Joan Miró") and [Antoni Tàpies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antoni_T%C3%A0pies "Antoni Tàpies") have signed [commemorative posters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poster "Poster"), just as Jaume Picas and the writer [Josep Maria Espinàs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Maria_Espin%C3%A0s "Josep Maria Espinàs"), on the occasion of the club's 75th anniversary, wrote the lyrics for _[Cant del Barça](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cant_del_Bar%C3%A7a "Cant del Barça")_ , the current anthem, with music by [Manuel Valls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Valls "Manuel Valls").[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-254)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-255)
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Al%C3%A8xia_Putellas_mural_163033.jpg/250px-Al%C3%A8xia_Putellas_mural_163033.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Al%C3%A8xia_Putellas_mural_163033.jpg)_[Follow my dreams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Follow_my_dreams "Follow my dreams")_ mural by Italian street artist [TVBoy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TVBoy "TVBoy"), this mural features [Barcelona Femení](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona_Femen%C3%AD "FC Barcelona Femení") player [Alexia Putellas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexia_Putellas "Alexia Putellas")
The Blaugrana world has also been a source of inspiration in the [plastic arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plastic_arts "Plastic arts"), with names such as Jordi Alumà, [Josep Maria Subirachs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Maria_Subirachs "Josep Maria Subirachs"), Antoni Tàpies or Josep Viladomat, who made the 'Avi del Barça' sculpture in the [La Masia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Masia "La Masia").[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-256) [Salvador Dalí](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salvador_Dal%C3%AD "Salvador Dalí") paid tribute to the club's 75th anniversary with an [etching](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Etching "Etching").[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-257)
In [performing arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Performing_arts "Performing arts"), [music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music "Music") has also been present, from the [tango](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tango "Tango") that [Gardel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlos_Gardel "Carlos Gardel") dedicated to [Samitier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Samitier "Josep Samitier") to the songs of [Joan Manuel Serrat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_Manuel_Serrat "Joan Manuel Serrat"), La Trinca and many others. [Theater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theatre "Theatre") has also been a good way to express the feelings of [Barça fans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supporters_of_FC_Barcelona#Fan_base "Supporters of FC Barcelona"), from the [El Paralelo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avinguda_del_Paral%C2%B7lel "Avinguda del Paral·lel") [cuplés](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cupl%C3%A9 "Cuplé") from before the [Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War "Spanish Civil War") or [skits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sketch_comedy "Sketch comedy") like 'El Partido del Domingo', by Castaños, to more recent texts, like _El culékulé_ , by [Xavier Bosch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xavier_Bosch_i_Sancho "Xavier Bosch i Sancho").[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-258)
In times of political difficulty or lack of freedoms, Barça has been a refuge and means of expression for cultural and [artistic activities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art "Art"). In 2013, the club highlighted the 'Barça Cultura' plan, an initiative that promotes the area of institutional relations and protocol with the aim of offering Barcelona as a platform to promote culture in Catalonia.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-259) In 2022, Barcelona and [Òmnium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%92mnium_Cultural "Òmnium Cultural") sign an agreement to promote the [Catalan language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalan_language "Catalan language"), culture and the [country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catalonia "Catalonia").[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-260)
There are many [documentaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Documentary_film "Documentary film") and [films](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film "Film") that have been created throughout history to capture the successes and journey of the club over the years. More recently, in December 2022, [Amazon Prime Video](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_Prime_Video "Amazon Prime Video") released a five-episode docuseries called _FC Barcelona: A New Era_.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-261) It documented the club by spending time with the coaching staff and players [behind the scenes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behind-the-scenes "Behind-the-scenes") both on and off the field throughout their [2021–22 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021%E2%80%9322_FC_Barcelona_season "2021–22 FC Barcelona season"). In September 2023, Amazon Prime Video launched the second season with a five-episode docuseries. It focuses on their [2022–23](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022%E2%80%9323_FC_Barcelona_season "2022–23 FC Barcelona season") behind the scenes season.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-262)
## Records
Further information: [List of FC Barcelona records and statistics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FC_Barcelona_records_and_statistics "List of FC Barcelona records and statistics")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/2012_2013_-_06_Xavi_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg/250px-2012_2013_-_06_Xavi_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2012_2013_-_06_Xavi_Hern%C3%A1ndez.jpg)[Xavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xavi_\(footballer,_born_1980\) "Xavi \(footballer, born 1980\)") made 767 total appearances for Barcelona, a former club record.
In March 2021, [Lionel Messi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lionel_Messi "Lionel Messi") overtook [Xavi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xavi_\(footballer,_born_1980\) "Xavi \(footballer, born 1980\)")'s record of 767 games played for the club, and presently has made 778 official appearances in all competitions, while also holding the record for the most appearances in La Liga matches for Barcelona, with 520.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-263)
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Leo_Messi_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Leo_Messi_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Leo_Messi_\(cropped\).jpg)[Lionel Messi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lionel_Messi "Lionel Messi") is Barcelona's all-time top appearance maker, top scorer, and the highest scoring player for a single club.
Barcelona's all-time highest goalscorer in official competitions is Lionel Messi with 672 goals, surpassing [César Rodríguez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_\(footballer,_born_1920\) "César Rodríguez \(footballer, born 1920\)")'s 232 goals in March 2012, a record which stood for 60 years.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-264) In December 2020, Messi also overtook [Pelé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pel%C3%A9 "Pelé")'s 643 goals for [Santos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santos_FC "Santos FC") to become the highest official scorer for a single club.[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-265) Messi is the record goalscorer for Barcelona in European and international club competitions,[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-individual-266) and the record league scorer with 474 goals in La Liga.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-267) Four [other players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FC_Barcelona_players "List of FC Barcelona players") have managed to score over 100 league goals for Barcelona: [César Rodríguez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Rodr%C3%ADguez_%C3%81lvarez "César Rodríguez Álvarez") (190), [Luis Suárez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luis_Su%C3%A1rez "Luis Suárez") (147), [László Kubala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%C3%A1szl%C3%B3_Kubala "László Kubala") (131) and [Samuel Eto'o](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samuel_Eto%27o "Samuel Eto'o") (108).[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-268) [Josep Samitier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Samitier "Josep Samitier") is the club's highest goalscorer in the [Copa del Rey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copa_del_Rey "Copa del Rey"), with 64 goals.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-269)
László Kubala holds the La Liga record for most goals scored in one match, with seven goals against [Sporting Gijón](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sporting_de_Gij%C3%B3n "Sporting de Gijón") in [1952](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1951%E2%80%9352_La_Liga "1951–52 La Liga").[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-270) Lionel Messi co-holds the [Champions League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League "UEFA Champions League") record with five goals against [Bayer Leverkusen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen "Bayer 04 Leverkusen") in [2012](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League "2011–12 UEFA Champions League").[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-271) [Eulogio Martínez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eulogio_Mart%C3%ADnez "Eulogio Martínez") became Barça's top goalscorer in a cup game, when he scored seven goals against Atlético Madrid in [1957](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1957_Copa_del_General%C3%ADsimo "1957 Copa del Generalísimo").[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-individual-266)
Barcelona goalkeepers have won a record number of [Zamora trophies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ricardo_Zamora_Trophy "Ricardo Zamora Trophy") (20), with [Antoni Ramallets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antoni_Ramallets "Antoni Ramallets") and [Víctor Valdés](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Vald%C3%A9s "Víctor Valdés") winning a record five each. Valdés had a ratio of 0.832 goals-conceded-per-game, a La Liga record,[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-272) and he also holds the record for longest period without conceding a goal (896 minutes) in all competitions for Barcelona.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-273) [Claudio Bravo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claudio_Bravo "Claudio Bravo") has the record of best unbeaten start in a season in La Liga history, at 754 minutes.[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-274)[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-275)
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Guardiola_2010.jpg/250px-Guardiola_2010.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Guardiola_2010.jpg)[Pep Guardiola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pep_Guardiola "Pep Guardiola") is Barcelona's most successful coach, with 14 trophies.
Barcelona's longest serving manager is [Jack Greenwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jack_Greenwell "Jack Greenwell"), with nine years in two spells (1917–1924) and (1931–1933), and [Pep Guardiola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pep_Guardiola "Pep Guardiola") is the club's most successful manager (14 trophies in 4 years). The most successful Barcelona player is Lionel Messi with 35 trophies, surpassing [Andrés Iniesta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Iniesta "Andrés Iniesta"), with 32 trophies.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-276)
Barcelona's Camp Nou is the [largest stadium in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_European_stadiums_by_capacity "List of European stadiums by capacity"). The club's highest home attendance was 120,000 in a European Cup quarter-final against Juventus on 3 March 1986.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-teamrecords-277) The modernisation of Camp Nou during the 1990s and the introduction of [all-seater stands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-seater_stadium "All-seater stadium") means the record will not be broken for the foreseeable future as the current capacity of the stadium is 99,354.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-278)
_El Barça de les Cinc Copes_ is the first team in Spanish football to have won five trophies in a single season (1951–1952).[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-279)[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-280)[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-281) Barcelona is the only club to have played in every season of European competitions since they started in 1955 counting non-[UEFA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UEFA "UEFA") competition Inter-Cities Fairs Cup.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-282)[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-283) On 18 December 2009, alongside being the only Spanish club to achieve a continental treble, Barcelona became the first ever European football team to win six trophies in a calendar year ([Sextuple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sextuple_\(association_football\) "Sextuple \(association football\)")).[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-284)[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-285) In January 2018, Barcelona signed [Philippe Coutinho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippe_Coutinho "Philippe Coutinho") from Liverpool for €120 million, the highest transfer fee in club's history.[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-286)[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-287) In August 2017, Barcelona player Neymar transferred to [Paris Saint-Germain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C. "Paris Saint-Germain F.C.") for a [world record](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_association_football_transfers#World_football_transfer_record "List of most expensive association football transfers") transfer fee of €222 million.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-288)[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-289)
In 2016, Barcelona's [La Masia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Masia "La Masia") was ranked second by the International Centre for Sports Studies (CIES) as the most top-level players producing academy in the world.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-290)
## Kits and crest
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Commons-logo.svg/40px-Commons-logo.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Commons-logo.svg)
Wikimedia Commons has media related to [FC Barcelona kits](https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona_kits "commons:FC Barcelona kits").
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Fc_barcelona_1st_badge_1899.png/120px-Fc_barcelona_1st_badge_1899.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fc_barcelona_1st_badge_1899.png)
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f8/FC_Barcelona_1910_logo.png/105px-FC_Barcelona_1910_logo.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:FC_Barcelona_1910_logo.png)
The first crest (left) worn by Barça from 1899 to 1910, and second crest (right), designed by Carles Comamala in 1910.
The club's original crest was a quartered diamond-shaped crest topped by the [Crown of Aragon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon "Crown of Aragon") and the [bat of King James](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bat_\(heraldry\)#The_bat_in_official_heraldry "Bat \(heraldry\)"), and surrounded by two branches, one of a laurel tree and the other a palm.[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-crest-32) The club shared [Barcelona's coat of arms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Barcelona "Coat of arms of Barcelona"), as a demonstration of its identification with the city and a desire to be recognised as one.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-291) In 1910, the club held a competition among its members to design a new crest. The winner was Carles Comamala, who at the time played for the club. Comamala's suggestion became the crest that the club wears today, with some minor variations. The crest consists of the [St George Cross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St_George%27s_Cross "St George's Cross") in the upper-left corner with the [Catalan flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senyera "Senyera") beside it, and the team colours at the bottom.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-292)
The blue and [garnet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shades_of_red#Garnet "Shades of red") colours of the shirt were first worn in a match against [Hispania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hispania "Hispania") in 1900.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-293) Several competing theories have been put forth for the blue and garnet design of the Barcelona shirt. The son of the first president, [Arthur Witty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Witty "Arthur Witty"), claimed it was the idea of his father as the colours were the same as the [Merchant Taylor's School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merchant_Taylors%27_School,_Crosby "Merchant Taylors' School, Crosby") team. Another explanation, according to author Toni Strubell, is that the colours are from Robespierre's [First Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_First_Republic "French First Republic"). In Catalonia the common perception is that the colours were chosen by Joan Gamper and are those of his home team, [FC Basel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Basel "FC Basel").[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-294)[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-295)

### Kit suppliers and shirt sponsors
Since 1998, the club has had a kit deal with [Nike](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nike,_Inc. "Nike, Inc."). In 2016, the deal was renewed until 2028 for a record €155 million per year. The contract includes a clause sanctioning penalty or agreement termination anytime if Barcelona fail to qualify for the European competitions or is relegated from [La Liga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Liga "La Liga").[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-307)[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-308) In 2023, Barcelona became the revenue leader from the sale of kits and merchandising in Europe with a turnover of €179 million.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-309)[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-310)
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Maillots_fc_barcelone.jpg/250px-Maillots_fc_barcelone.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Maillots_fc_barcelone.jpg)Nike has been Barcelona's official kit supplier since 1998.
Although Spanish clubs first began displaying sponsor names on their shirts in 1981,[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-311) Barcelona held off having a name across the front of the shirt until 2006, when the club signed an agreement to have [UNICEF](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNICEF "UNICEF")'s name on their front.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-312)[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-313) Unlike traditional deals, this was not to have paying money to the club, but instead to have the club raise money for UNICEF. In 2011, the club signed its first commercial shirt sponsorship deal, when it reached an agreement with [Qatar Foundation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qatar_Foundation "Qatar Foundation").[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-qatar-314)

## Anthems
Further information: [Cant del Barça](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cant_del_Bar%C3%A7a "Cant del Barça")
Throughout its history, the club has had various official songs. The anthem in use today is "Cant del Barça" (The Song of Barça), composed in 1974 on the occasion of the club's 75th anniversary. Authors [Josep Maria Espinàs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josep_Maria_Espin%C3%A0s "Josep Maria Espinàs") and [Jaume Picas](https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaume_Picas_i_Guiu "ca:Jaume Picas i Guiu") composed the lyrics in Catalan, while the music was composed by [Manuel Valls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuel_Valls_\(composer\) "Manuel Valls \(composer\)").[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-321)[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-322)
The song was first performed on 27 November 1974 at [Camp Nou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_Nou "Camp Nou") before the match between FC Barcelona and the East Germany national team by a 3,500-man choir led by [Oriol Martorell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oriol_Martorell_i_Codina "Oriol Martorell i Codina"). On November 28, 1988, in celebration of the club's centenary, the song was performed by Catalan singer-songwriter [Joan Manuel Serrat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joan_Manuel_Serrat "Joan Manuel Serrat") at the end of the festival at Camp Nou. Since the 2008–09 season, el Cant del Barça has been featured on the official Barcelona jerseys.
On the occasion of the club's 124th anniversary and with the start of preparations for the 125th anniversary, the club presented a new anthem version recording faithful to the essence of the original score and lyrics composed in 1974, with a better quality and enhanced orchestration and vocals. Composed by the [Vallès Symphony Orchestra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vall%C3%A8s_Symphony_Orchestra "Vallès Symphony Orchestra"), the [Orfeó Català](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orfe%C3%B3_Catal%C3%A0 "Orfeó Català") choral society and the Cor Jove youth choir, it is the current official version.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-323)[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-324)
El Cant del Barça is turned on before Barcelona games take place at Camp Nou, especially during matches against Real Madrid and just before the start of the meeting. The song is also often played for supporters and fans to cheer, chant and celebrate the victory.
## Stadium
Main articles: [Camp de la Indústria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_de_la_Ind%C3%BAstria "Camp de la Indústria"), [Camp de Les Corts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_de_Les_Corts "Camp de Les Corts"), and [Camp Nou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_Nou "Camp Nou")
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/LesCortes1939.jpg/250px-LesCortes1939.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LesCortes1939.jpg)[Camp de Les Corts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_de_Les_Corts "Camp de Les Corts") in 1939. It was the home stadium for Barcelona until the club moved to Camp Nou in 1957.
Barcelona initially played on different fields, one of the first to represent a fixed venue was the Camp de la Indústria. The capacity was about 6,000, and club officials deemed the facilities inadequate for a club with growing membership.[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-325)
In 1922, the number of supporters had surpassed 20,000 and by lending money to the club, Barça was able to build the larger Camp de Les Corts, which had an initial capacity of 20,000 spectators. After the Spanish Civil War the club started attracting more members and a larger number of spectators at matches. This led to several expansion projects: the grandstand in 1944, the southern stand in 1946, and finally the northern stand in 1950. After the last expansion, Les Corts could hold 60,000 spectators.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-fcbarcelona6-326)
After the construction was complete there was no further room for expansion at Les Corts. Back-to-back La Liga titles in 1948 and 1949 and the signing of László Kubala in June 1950, who would later go on to score 196 goals in 256 matches, drew larger crowds to the games.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-fcbarcelona6-326)[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-327)[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-328) The club began to make plans for a new stadium.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-fcbarcelona6-326) The building of Camp Nou commenced on 28 March 1954, before a crowd of 60,000 Barça fans. The first stone of the future stadium was laid in place under the auspices of Governor Felipe Acedo Colunga and with the blessing of Archbishop of Barcelona Gregorio Modrego. Construction took three years and ended on 24 September 1957 with a final cost of 288 million [pesetas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_peseta "Spanish peseta"), 336% over budget.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-fcbarcelona6-326)
[![The words "Més que un club" are painted in yellow on the blue seats of the stadium](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/CampNouMotto.jpg/250px-CampNouMotto.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CampNouMotto.jpg)One of the [Camp Nou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_Nou "Camp Nou") stands displays Barcelona's motto, _"Més que un club"_ , meaning 'More than a club'.
In 1980, when the stadium was in need of redesign to meet UEFA criteria, the club raised money by offering supporters the opportunity to inscribe their name on the bricks for a small fee. The idea was popular with supporters, and thousands of people paid the fee. Later this became the centre of controversy when media in Madrid picked up reports that one of the stones was inscribed with the name of long-time Real Madrid chairman and Franco supporter Santiago Bernabéu.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-329)[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-330)[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-331) In preparation for the [1992 Summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics "1992 Summer Olympics") two tiers of seating were installed above the previous roofline.[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-332) It has a current capacity of 99,354 making it the largest stadium in Europe.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-stadium-333)
In December 2021, a record 88% of the club members voted in favor of the _Espai Barça_ project to revamp the club's sporting facilities, being the first online referendum in FC Barcelona history.[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-334) Originally projected to have been completed in 2021, renovation work on Camp Nou began on 1 June 2023 and it is now aimed to finish by the end of 2026, with an estimated €1.5 billion net funding.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-335)[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-336)[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-337) During the renovation period, Barcelona will move for the entire [2023–24 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023%E2%80%9324_FC_Barcelona_season "2023–24 FC Barcelona season") to [Estadi Olímpic Lluís Companys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estadi_Ol%C3%ADmpic_Llu%C3%ADs_Companys "Estadi Olímpic Lluís Companys") in Montjuïc, expecting to return in November 2024, with the stadium still under construction.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-338)
There are also other facilities, which include:[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-339)
  * [Ciutat Esportiva Joan Gamper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ciutat_Esportiva_Joan_Gamper "Ciutat Esportiva Joan Gamper") (FC Barcelona's training ground)
  * [Masia-Centre de Formació Oriol Tort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_Masia "La Masia") (Residence of young players)
  * [Estadi Johan Cruyff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estadi_Johan_Cruyff "Estadi Johan Cruyff") (Home of the [reserve team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona_Atl%C3%A8tic "FC Barcelona Atlètic"), [women's team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona_Femen%C3%AD "FC Barcelona Femení"), and [Juvenil A](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona_\(youth\) "FC Barcelona \(youth\)"))
  * [Palau Blaugrana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palau_Blaugrana "Palau Blaugrana") (FC Barcelona indoor sports arena)
  * Palau Blaugrana 2 (Secondary indoor arena of FC Barcelona)

## Players
Main article: [List of FC Barcelona players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_FC_Barcelona_players "List of FC Barcelona players")
For a list of all former and current FC Barcelona players with a Wikipedia article, see [Category:FC Barcelona players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:FC_Barcelona_players "Category:FC Barcelona players").
Spanish teams are limited to three players without EU citizenship. The squad list includes only the principal nationality of each player; several non-European players on the squad have [dual citizenship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiple_citizenship "Multiple citizenship") with an EU country. Also, players from the [ACP countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ACP_countries "ACP countries") that are signatories to the [Cotonou Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cotonou_Agreement "Cotonou Agreement") are not counted against non-EU quotas due to the [Kolpak ruling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kolpak_ruling "Kolpak ruling").[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FC_Barcelona#cite_note-341)
Further information: [2024–25 FC Barcelona season § Players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024%E2%80%9325_FC_Barcelona_season#Players "2024–25 FC Barcelona season")
